Jamison Brereton

70 (679)
Indra
Puruhanman ─Ас╣Еgirasa
15 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л arranged in prag─Бthas 1тАУ6; br╠еhat─л arranged in trcas 7тАУ12; u ╠е с╣гс╣Зih 13, anuс╣гс╣нubh 14, pura├╝с╣гс╣Зih 15
Another metrically complex hymn. The first six verses consist of three prag─Бthas in br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, the next six (7тАУ12) of two tr╠еcas in br╠еhat─л, and the last three (13тАУ15) of verses in three different meters, but all consisting of eight syl lable or a mixture of eight and twelve syllable lines, like the br╠еhat─л/satobr╠еhat─л verses before them.
The thematic divisions correspond well with these metrical divisions. The first six verses are extravagant praise of IndraтАЩs unequalled power. Having flat tered him with his praise, the poet occupies the tr╠еca portion with the usual requests for Indra to exercise his generosity and, more strikingly, for him to pun ish mortals who do not worship him and do not follow the ─Аrya way, with the culminating verse 11 listing the numerous ways in which this evil man can deviate from the proper path. One of the stylistic features especially of the tr╠еca section (but see also vs. 4) is the tendency for the final word or words of the c and d p─Бdas to match (4cd, 7cd, 8cd, 11cd, 12cd; see also 9a+d), and there are other verse-internal echoes.
The final three verses (13тАУ15) are a d─Бnastuti of ┼Ъara ┼Ъauradevya, or rather what we might term an anti-d─Бnastuti or, technically, a satire. The first of these verses (13) poses a rhetorical question that seems to promise lavish praise to come, but the poet takes this back in verse 14 with another rhetorical question: will you really receive praise for a gift that consists of calves doled out in miserly fashion? The final verse specifies just how miserly: a single calf for three poets. In these verses the standard vocabulary of generosity (benefactor, patron, bounteous one) is deployed sarcasti
cally, and the poet cleverly gives his criticism a gloss of praise.
For an analysis of the phonetic and grammatical features of the entire hymn, see Watkins (1995: 184тАУ87).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI praise that Indra who is the lord of men, who proceeds irresistible in his chariots, the breaker-throughof all armies, the pre-eminent one, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tarut─Б = t─Бrakaс╕е, deliverer; (RV 8.1.21): conqueror

Jamison Brereton

He who is king of the separate peoples, a driver with chariots, rich, an overcomer in all battles, who is sung as the preeminent smasher of Vr╠еtraтАФ

Griffith

HE who, as Sovran Lord of men, moves with his chariots unrestrained,
The Vrtra-slayer vanquisher, of fighting hosts, preeminent, is praised with song.

Geldner

Grassmann

Ihn, der der Menschen K├╢nig ist, auf Wagen unaufhaltsam f├дhrt, Den Schlachtensieger preise ich, den besten Vritrat├╢dter ihn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPuruhanman, honour that Indra for your protection, for in your upholder there is a two-fold might; heholds in his hand (to smite his enemies) the glorious thunderbolt great as the sun in heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Two-fold might: tosmite your enemies and to favour your friends

Jamison Brereton

Beautify that Indra, o Puruhanman, for his help, him whose (mace) is once again in (the hand of) the apportioner:
the mace, lovely to see, has been put back into his hand, like the great sun into heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бdas b and c are difficult. The superficially most natural interpretation is to take the two together, as Geldner does (тАЬin dessen Hand тАж die gerngesehene Keule gelegt wardтАжтАЭ; so also Oldenberg), but the putative verb in this relative clause, dh─Бyi in c, is unaccented. If we take this lack of accent seriously, and I think we should, some other solution has to be found for the relative clause in p─Бda b, a task made all the more challenging by the disputed form vidhart├бri. This particular form appears twice (also IX.47.4) and formally belongs to the agent noun vidhart├бr- (voc. sg. 1x, nom. sg. 4x) тАШdistributor, apportionerтАЩ. The -t├бri forms are nonetheless generally taken as infinitives. Tichy (1995: 59-61), by contrast, takes them as loc. sg. of a verbal abstract (here тАЬin dessen Hand, wenn es ans Verteilen geht, ein weiteres Mal die sehenswerte Keule gelegt wirdтАЭ [p. 60]), and others take it as nom. sg. neut. (See disc.

of these various possibilities with earlier lit. in Oldenberg and in Keydana [Infin. 196-99].) Keydana, at least for this verse, suggests that vidhart├бri is the (infinitival?) subject of the nominal relative clause, y├бsya its specifier, and dvit─Б╠Бa predicate adverb: тАЬDer Hand wurde die Keule dargereicht (p─Бda c), deren Austeilung ein weiteres Mal [erfolgt] (p─Бda b)тАЭ (199 n. 31). I consider the form to be a locative (like Tichy), but a locative not to an abstract but to the agent noun it appears to be and coreferential with Indra in p─Бda a. Alternatively it could refer to a third party, who is responsible for the return of IndraтАЩs mace; this seems to be OldenbergтАЩs favored solution: тАЬbeim (Welt)ordner,тАЭ who is responsible for equipping Indra with the mace. In the absence of mythical context we cannot be certain. Though I have added the parenthetical тАЬ(in the hand of),тАЭ this tr. is an English makeshift for the German bei or French chez, which both render such locatives more efficiently. The statement in b, that the mace has been returned to Indra, is then restated in p─Бda c more clearly.

The datives h├бst─Бya and div├й instead of the locatives that might be expected are curious.

Griffith

Honour that Indra, Puruhanman! for his aid, in whose sustaining hand of old,
The splendid bolt of thunder was deposited, as the great Sun was set in heaven.

Geldner

Den Indra verherrliche, o Puruhanman, zur Gunsterweisung, in dessen Hand, um sie festzuhalten, abermals die gerngesehene Keule gelegt ward wie die gro├Яe Sonne an den Himmel.

Grassmann

Den Indra stimme, Puruhanman, dir zum Schutz, in dessen Hand als seine Wehr Der sch├╢ne Blitz gelegt ward, wie ans Himmelszelt der hocherhabne Sonnengott.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNone can touch him by his deeds, who has made Indra his friend by sacrifices– (Indra) ever givingfresh strength, to be hymned by all, great, unconquered, of ever-daring might.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

No one will catch up with him who by his (ritual?) action created an ever strengthening one
like Indra, welcomed with sacrifices by all, ingenious, unassailable but of assailing might,

Jamison Brereton Notes

The identity of тАЬhimтАЭ in тАЬNo one will catch up with himтАжтАЭ is not sufficiently signalled in the published translation I take it to refer to the successful sacrificer (cf. VIII.31.17), who ritually strengthens and thus тАЬhas createdтАЭ Indra. However, the perfect cak─Б╠Бra could instead signal mythic time; both Geldner and Oldenberg believe this refers to the original creator of Indra, as in IV.17.4. The reference to IndraтАЩs birth in 4cd may support their position.

Griffith

No one by deed attains to him who works and strengthens evermore:
No, not by sacrifice, to Indra. praised o all, resistless, daring, bold in might.

Geldner

Keiner kommt dem an Verdienst gleich, der einen stets F├╢rdernden wie den Indra erzeugt hat, den mit Opfergebeten Allgepriesenen, Meisterlichen, Unangreifbaren, von k├╝hner Kraft.

Grassmann

Ihm kommt an Werken keiner gleich, die er gethan, dem segnenden, Dem vielgeliebten Indra an Verehrung nicht, der stark ist, k├╝hn und unbesiegt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(I laud) him who is not to be withstood, the mighty, the conqueror in hostile hosts; whom, when he wasborn, the strong rushing cows welcomed and the heavens and the earths praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kс╣г─Бmaс╕е = kс╣гamiс╕е;

Rushingcows: Maruts, the sons of Pс╣Ы┼Ыni; or, mankind offering oblations of clarified butteс╣Ы..; the earths: the worlds arethree-fold, trivс╣Ыto lokaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Invincible, mighty, and victorious in battles, in whose (control) are the great, wide-expanding (waters?).
While he was being born, the milk-cows kept bellowing in unison; the heavens and earths kept bellowing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In my view this verse is structurally parallel to vs. 2: p─Бda a continues the previous verse; b is a nominal relative clause; and cd may or may not go with b, but have unaccented verbs. Geldner (n. to 2b) and Oldenberg also consider the verses parallel, but in the case of both verses they think that bc belong together despite the unaccented verbs of c(d). In separating b and c here I must supply a noun with the fem.

adjectives mah─л╠Бr urujr├бyaс╕е – and choose тАШwatersтАЩ, since pl. ─Б╠Бpas, ap├бs is common with mah─л╠Бс╕е; тАШriversтАЩ would also be possible, so Geldner, who seems to take mah─л╠Бс╕е simply as a designation of rivers (тАЬdie breitstr├╢menden Fl├╝sseтАЭ) without comment.

Griffith

The potent Conqueror, invincible in war, him at whose birth the Mighty Ones,
The Kine who spread aftar, sent their loud voices out, heavens, earths seat their loud voices out,

Geldner

Den Unbezwungenen, Gewaltigen, in den Schlachten Bezwingenden, bei dessen Geburt die breitstr├╢menden Fl├╝sse, die Milchk├╝he zusammen br├╝llten, die Himmel, die Erden br├╝llten.

Grassmann

Der unbesiegt in Schlachten siegt, der m├дchtige, bei dess Geburt die K├╝he schon Die ausgedehnten, grossen alle jubelten, und Erd’ und Himmel jubelten.

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

If a 100 Heavens o indra,
as also a 100 Earths could be yours,
O vajrin, a 1000 suns were not equal to you
even as you were born, nor were world-hemispheres.

shleSha in aShTa- indicating holy numbers 100+8; 1000+8 though in terms of semantics I believe it is the modal verb from root ash

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, were there a hundred heavens to compare with you, or were there a hundred earths– Othunderer, not even a thousand suns woudl reveal you– yes, no created thing would fill you, nor heaven andearth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Not even a thousand suns: there (in br─Бhmaс╣Зa) the sun shines not: Katha Upan. 5.15; no created thing would fill you: the soul within my heart is greater than the earth, greater than the sky, greater than the heaven,greater than all these worlds: Ch─Бndogya Up. 3.14

Jamison Brereton

Since a hundred heavens and a hundred earths could be yours, Indra, a thousand suns were not equal to you when you were just born, o mace-bearer, nor were the two world-halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The conjoined NPs in ab display a neat chiasmus: dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е тАж ┼Ыat├бс╣Г, ┼Ыat├бm bh┼л╠Бm─лс╕е. This may help account for the placement of the ut├б after the second term (indeed after the entire second term: ┼Ыat├бm bh┼л╠Бm─лr ut├б). Although XY ut├б structures are by no means uncommon (see Klein DGRV I.344-53), they are considerably rarer than the standard X ut├б Y type.

In cd there are two parallel nominal subjects, pl. sah├бsraс╣Г s┼л╠Бry─Бс╕е and du.

r├│das─л, and neither matches the sg. verb ├бnu тАж aс╣гс╣нa in number. Several solutions have been proposed. BR (see Oldenberg) and Grassmann take r├│das─л as singular, but all other examples of sg. r├│das─л (and more common rodas─л╠Б) refer to the goddess of that name; when r├│das─л refers to the world-halves, it is always dual. Oldenberg also cites Geldner Komm for the view that the sg. verb was influenced by sah├бsram. I am inclined to assume that the sg. verb split the difference between the plural and dual subjects, and it is also possible that the construction was somehow syntactically calqued on the inherited neuter plural subject + singular verb construction (though neither of the subjects is neuter). ItтАЩs also worth noting that the root aor. 3rd du. middle of тИЪ(n)a┼Ы is not attested, and in fact, acdg. to Macdonell, Vedic Grassmann, the only 2nd or 3rd du. mid. root aor. attested is adh─лt─Бm (X.4.6, тИЪdh─Б) – so the poet may have been a bit insecure about what the du. form ought to be (*a┼Ы─Бt─Бm? *aс╣гс╣н─Бс╣Г?), and the pl. s┼л╠Бry─Бс╕е may have been too distant in the vs. to allow the 3rd pl. a┼Ыata to be used instead.

Griffith

O Indra, if a hundred heavens and if a hundred earths were thine-
No, not a thousand Suns could match thee at thy birth, not both the worlds, O Thunderer.

Wenn, Indra, hundert Himmel dir und hundert Erden w├дren auch, So fassten tausend Sonnen nicht dich, Blitzender, nicht das Geschaffne, Welten nicht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMightiest showerer (of blessings), you have filled all (our hosts) with your vast bountiful power; OMaghavan, thunderer, guard us with your manifold protections, (when we march) against the well-stockedcowpen of our enemies.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You have filled all things with your bullish greatness, bull, and with your strength, strongest one.
Help us to a pen full of cattle with your bright help, bounteous
mace-bearer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes the loc. g├│mati vraj├й as a loc. absolute (тАЬwenn es sich um rindergef├╝llte H├╝rde handeltтАЭ). By using the Engl. idiom тАЬhelp someone to somethingтАЭ I may be stretching Sanskrit syntax further than is legitimate. Though see Grassmann, definition 4 s.v. av: тАЬjemandem [A.] wozu [D., L.] verhelfen.тАЭ Unfortunately this is the only passage he places under that rubric with a loc.; the others have datives.

However, in Rivelex vol. I the Deep Case Frame for avi , subsection 1d / 1da, tags a number of other possible such passages with this structure (not all of which I would so interpret).

Griffith

Thou, Hero, hast performed thy hero deeds with might, yea, all with strength, O Strongest One.
Maghavan, help us to a stable full of kine, O Thunderer, with wondrous aids.

Geldner

Du hast mit deiner Gr├╢├Яe, deiner Bullenkraft, du Bulle, mit deiner Macht, du M├дchtigster, alle R├дume erf├╝llt. Steh uns bei, Gabenreicher, wenn es sich um rindergef├╝llte H├╝rde handelt, mit deinen wunderbaren Hilfen, Keulentr├дger!

Grassmann

Mit Macht hast du dein Heldenwerk erf├╝llt, o Held, mit St├дrke alles, st├дrkster du; Verhilf, o m├дcht’ger, uns zu rinderreichem Stall, mit reichen H├╝lfen, Blitzender.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO long-lived Indra, the mortal who has not you as his deity obtains no food; (he who praises not) thatsteed-borne Indra, who yokes to his car the two variegated, who yokes the two bay steeds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аpas = apa tad;har─л indraс╕е = indro hari

Jamison Brereton

A godless mortal shall not acquire refreshment, o long-lived one!
Indra, who will yoke his two steeds that win dappled cows, who will yoke his two fallow baysтАФ1164 VIII.71

Jamison Brereton Notes

For ├йtagva- as тАШwinning dappled cowsтАЩ, see Thieme, Studien 67-68 and EWA s.v. The second hemistich is unconnected to the first; its two rel. clauses attach to the next verse.

Griffith

Let not a godless mortal gain this food, O thou whose life is long!
But one who yokes the bright-hued steeds, the Etasas, even Indra yoker of the Bays.

Geldner

Nicht soll der gottlose Sterbliche Speisegenu├Я erlangen, o Langlebiger! Welcher Indra sogar die beiden buntfarbigen Etasarosse anschirrt, die Hari┬┤s anschirrt,

Grassmann

Kein Sterblicher, der gottlos ist, hat Gut erlangt, Unsterblicher; Nur der erlangt’s, der dir die schnellen Rosse schirrt, das F├╝chsepaar, o Indra, schirrt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGreat (priests), worship that Indra who is propitiated by gifts; who is to be invoked in the shallows andin the depths, and who is to be invoked in battles.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Propitiated by gifts: d─Бn─Бya sakс╣гaс╣Зim = who follows for agift

Jamison Brereton

(Call upon) him to give to youтАФIndra, the conqueror to be greatly magnified,
who is to be called upon at the fords and in foreign parts, who is to be called upon at the prize-contests.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though as just noted, 7cd should be construed with this verse, the main clause to which those rel. clauses should be attached is incomplete - having a referent t├бm for the y├бс╕е of 7c, but no main verb. Geldner supplies тАЬrufet,тАЭ which seems the simplest solution, extracted from the two forms of h├бvyaс╕е in cd.

Grassmann, Geldner take ─Б╠Бraс╣Зa- as тАШdepthsтАЩ, presumably as a contextual antonym to g─Б╠Бdha- тАШfordтАЩ, putatively тЖР *тАШshallowтАЩ (but see EWA s.v.). But there seems no good reason to separate ─Б╠Бraс╣Зa- from ├бraс╣Зa- тАШalien, foreignтАЩ and its relatives, esp. since a ford is a тАШshallowтАЩ only indirectly. The other occurrence of ─Б╠Бraс╣Зa- (I.112.6) is not in an antonymic context; Geldner renders it тАЬin der GrubeтАЭ (pit), but there is no external support for this tr.

Griffith

Urge ye the Conqueror to give, your Indra greatly to be praised,
To be invoked in shallow waters and in depths, to be invoked in deeds of might.

Geldner

Diesen herrlichen, zu verherrlichenden, siegreichen Indra rufet zum Schenken, der in Untiefen und Tiefen anzurufen ist, der in den Preisk├дmpfen anzurufen ist.

Grassmann

Ihn, euren hehren Indra treibt, den Sieger, viel zu schenken uns, Den man an seichtem und den man an tiefem Ort, Den man in Schlachten rufen muss.

English translation:

тАЬO hero, giver of dwellings, raise up to enjoy abundant food; raise us up, Maghavan, for abundantwealth; raise us up, Indra, for abundant fame.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Shape us up for your great generosity, o good one, championтАФ
(shape us) up for your great giving of bounty, bounteous one; (shape us) up for great fame, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme ud тИЪmс╣Ы┼Ы is found only here in early Vedic, but like other combinations of тИЪmс╣Ы┼Ы тАШtouchтАЩ + preverb, it seems to have a slightly slangy sense. Grassmann тАЬjemand [A.] emporheben zu [D.],тАЭ but the sense of touch is lost. Geldner тАЬStreck fein (die Hand) f├╝r uns aus,тАЭ which fails to render both the root meaning and the preverb.

My тАЬshape us upтАЭ attempts to render both, with the sense тАЬmake us ready/worthy to receive.тАЭ The insistent ├║d here, opening p─Бdas a, c, and d, may be meant to contrast with n├н in the following verse (p─Бdas b, d).

Note the alliteration: ab тАж mah├й, mс╣Ы┼Ыasva тАж and esp. cd тАж mahya├н maghavan magh├бttaye, тАж mah├й# This is the culmination of a play on mah- and magha- forms in the central part of the hymn: 6a mahin─Б╠Б, 6c maghavan, 8a mah├│ mah─Б╠Бyyam.

Griffith

O Vasu, O thou Hero, raise us up to ample opulence.
Raise us to gain of mighty wealth, O Maghavan, O Indra, to sublime renown.

Streck fein die Hand f├╝r uns aus, du Guter, zu gro├Яer Freigebigkeit, du Held, zu gro├Яer Gabe, du Gabenreicher, zu gro├Яem Ruhme, Indra!

Grassmann

O hebe, guter, uns empor, zu grossem Schatze schnell, o Held, Empor, o reicher, uns zu reichem Schatzempfang, Idra, empor zu hohem Ruhm.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, who delights in offerings, you satisfy us abundantly with (the possession of him) who despisesyou; O you possessed of vast wealth, shelter us between your thighs; you smite down the D─Бsa with yourblows.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You are the one who seeks the truth for us, Indra. You find no
satisfaction in him who reviles you.
Gird yourself in between your thighs, o you of mighty manliness. Jab down the D─Бsa with your blows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme n├н тИЪtс╣Ыp occurs only here (in all of Sanskrit, as far as I can tell). I interpret the n├н as reversing the meaning of the root verb, as sometimes elsewhere (see Jamison 1983: 86 for some other examples) - hence тАШbe unsatisfiedтАЩ тЖР тИЪtс╣Ыp тАШbe satisfiedтАЩ. Scarlatta also seems to interpret the verb in this fashion (тАЬтАж bist du unzufriedenтАЭ), but does not comment on why. Grassmann тАШverzehrenтАЩ (consume), Oldenberg тАШsich s├дttigenтАЩ. Since tс╣Ыmp├бti is ordinarily construed with a genitive, I take tv─Бn├нdaс╕е as a gen. sg., not acc. pl., as Grassmann and Geldner take it. Scarlatta allows either possibility, and Oldenberg favors the gen. My interpretation is thus rather distinct from GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdu hast deine Schm├дher sattтАЭ (have your fill of), though his also conveys a negative sense.

The girding motif of c must indicate some kind of preparation for battle, but what exactly the equipment and procedure were is not clear.

I have, reluctantly, interpreted the injunctive ┼Ыi┼Ыnathaс╕е in d as an imperative, as also in VIII.24.25. So also Geldner in both passages. It would be possible here (less so in VIII.24.25) to interpret it modally тАЬyou will jab downтАжтАЭ or even as a timeless statement тАЬyou jab downтАжтАЭ Note the play of #t u v├бmтАж, #t u van├нdo тАж / тАж tuvinс╣Ыmna

Griffith

Indra, thou justifiest us, and tramplest down thy slanderers.
Guard thyself, valiant Hero, in thy vital parts: strike down the Dasa with thy blows.

Geldner

Du, Indra, willst uns gerecht werden, du hast deine Schm├дher satt. Bedecke dich, du Mutiger, zwischen den Schenkeln, schlag den Dasa mit deinen Streichen nieder!

Grassmann

Du Indra bist uns Frommen hold, den, der dich hasst, verzehrest du; Dem D├дmon ziele mitten auf die H├╝ften hin, mit Todesschuss durchbohre ihn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your friend, Parvata, hurl down from heaven him who follows other rites, the enemy of men, himwho offers no sacrifice and who worships not the gods; may Parvata hurl the Dasyu down to the storm smiter(death).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Parvata: (RV 1.122.3): Parjanya; (RV 7.37.8): a god, a friend of INdra; here, he is a с╣Ыс╣гi, a friend of Indra,tava sakhi bh┼лtaс╕е Parvata с╣Ыс╣гiс╕е; enemy of men: am─Бnuс╣гam = the enemy of the men who sacrifice to Indra

Jamison Brereton

The man who follows other commandments, who is no son of Manu, no sacrificer, no devotee of the godsтАФ
him should your own comrade, the mountain [=mace?], send tumbling down; the mountain (should send down) the Dasyu for easy smiting.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes the sv├бс╕е s├бkh─Б to refer to the enemyтАЩs comrade, but given the dual dvandva voc. ├нndr─Бparvat─Б (3x) тАЬo Indra and Mountain,тАЭ it seems more likely to be IndraтАЩs. In those passages I take тАЬmountainтАЭ as a designation of IndraтАЩs mace.

Griffith

The man who brings no sacrifice, inhuman, godless, infidel,
Him let his friend the mountain cast to rapid death, the mountain cast the Dasyu down.

Geldner

Ihn, der andere Gebote befolgt, den Unmenschen, der nicht opfert, den Gottlosen, soll sein Freund Berg absch├╝tteln, der Berg den Dasyu, da├Я er leicht zu erschlagen sei.

Grassmann

Wer G├╢tzen dient, unmenschlich ist, wer Opfer nicht noch G├╢tter liebt, Den st├╝rz’ herab der eigne Fels auf den er traut, den Feind zu schnellem Tod der Fels.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMost powerful Indra, in your favour towards us, take these cows in your hand, as fried grain, to give tous; yes, take them twice in your favour towards us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O strongest Indra, grab a handful of these (cows), o most capacious one, to give to us,
like a handful of roasted grains, being disposed toward us. Grab two, being disposed toward us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

IndraтАЩs generous handful of cows in this final verse before the sarcastic d─Бnastuti implicitly contrasts with the stinginess of ┼Ъara, who gives only one calf (vs. 15).

Griffith

O Mightiest Indra, loving us, gather thou up, as grains of corn,
Within thine hand, of these their kine, to give away, yea, gather twice as loving us.

Geldner

Von diesen K├╝hen nimm, Indra, als w├дren es K├╢rner, die Hand voll uns zuliebe, um uns zu schenken, du M├дchtigster, doppelt nimm uns zuliebe!

Grassmann

O Indra, nimm in deine Hand wie Gerstenk├╢rner Sch├дtze doch, Sie uns zu geben, o du st├дrkster, holdgesinnt, zweimal erfasse sie uns hold.

English translation:

тАЬAssociated priests, give good heed to the sacrifice, for how can we (worthily) perform the praise of(Indra) the destroyer, who is the recompenser of enemies, the sender of reward, the unvanquished?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Therecompenser: bhojaс╕е = ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm bhojayit─Б; (RV 8.3.24): the despoiler of enemies; (RV 2.14.10): phalasyad─Бt─Бram rakс╣гit─Бram ca

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, the common object of our worship, you are praised by many sacrificing с╣Ъс╣гis; for it is you,destroyer of foes, who thus give calves in succession to your worshippers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In succession: ekam ekam = one byone, i.e., many;

Calves = calves and cow

Jamison Brereton

Will you be praised in any way by many seers provided with ritual grass, ┼Ъara, if you will hand over your calves in just this way, one by one?

Griffith

By many a sage whose grass is trimmed thou art continually praised,
That thou, O Sara, hast bestowed here one and here another’calf.

Geldner

Von vielen opfernden Rishi┬┤s wirst du jedenfalls gepriesen werden, wenn du, Sara, also die K├дlber, jedesmal eines, verschwendest.

Grassmann

Von vielen S├дngern, die mit Streu versehn sind, wirst du vielfach gepriesen werden, weil du, o ├Зara, einen nach dem andern mit K├дlbern beschenktest.

English translation:

тАЬMay Maghavan, taking them by the ears, lead the cows with their calves from our three (destructiveenemies), as the owner leads a goat to drink.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vatsam naс╕е = vatsam naс╕е, vatsa sahitaс╕е;

Sauradevaс╕е = cow, i.e.connected with or won in battle (sauradevam)

Jamison Brereton

The bounteous son of ┼Ъ┼лradeva, having grabbed hold of its ear, led a calf here to us three,
a patron (leading) a nanny-goat to give suck (to three kids).

Jamison Brereton Notes

See comment on 12. The thematic connection between the verses is underscored by the presence of the verb тАШgrabтАЩ in each, but note that vs. 15, part of the hymn proper, has the older form тИЪgrabh (s├бс╣Г gс╣Ыbh─Бya), while the d─Бnastuti, belonging to a more popular level of language, has the younger тИЪgrah (-gс╣Ы╠Бhya).

Griffith

The noble, Suradeva’s son, hath brought a calf, led by the car to three of us.
As a chief brings a goat to milk.
